Ailia had a really hard time figuring out what she was saying. Ivanka’s accent was too strong to understand at moments and the meaning of her words, difficult to grasp. “Will you read my future now?” she said.
“Come with me.” Ivanka gestured and held open the tent entrance. Dozens of candles lit the tent and had transformed it into a hot and smoky dancing cave of shadows. Ivanka sat down in her chair. “Sit,” Ivanka ordered Ailia, moving her chair to the other side of the table.
Ailia sat down on the same stool she had sat on earlier in the day and leaned forward. I must be crazy to try this again, she thought.
“Left hand, please,” Ivanka instructed, reaching out for it. She was not wasting any time. She took two deep breaths again and said the same foreign words she had before, just faster. She then opened her eyes and her demeanor had changed.
“Now, let me see.” She studied Ailia’s palm. “Yes, I see, I see, good—not good. Hmm—” She was nodding and shaking her head interchangeably. “Ah, your palm is not able to be read, except for you have three lives, one love. Cannot see which life you are living now—three is too much. Other hand,” she said and let go of Ailia’s left hand. 
Ailia extended her right arm and opened her palm. 
“Hmmm,” Ivanka said. “Hmmm—” She turned Ailia’s hand around and clasped it. “Not tonight, dearie. You make your own destiny. You find it in here,” she said and pointed her long, dirt-infested fingernail into Ailia’s chest. “— here,” she said and pointed to Ailia's forehead. “You may or may not win.” 
“What?” Ailia asked. That was no more or less than she already knew.
“Remember, truth is inside you, buried down deep. Your spirit creates all wonders,” Ivanka said and stood up. “No need to look elsewhere than inside.” She blew out a dozen candles and then looked at Ailia. “No more tonight, good night.”
Ailia stood up and slowly walked out of the tent miles more confused than when she had walked in. 
“One more thing—” The fortuneteller said. “He will be here tonight.”
“Who?” Ailia said. Soren?
“Good night.” Ivanka shut the tent door without another word. 
Nothing made sense. Ivanka seemed like she knew what she was talking about, but why wouldn’t she share what she had seen? Whose side is she on anyhow? It had been a rather unsatisfactory adventure, incapable of answering Ailia’s important questions. 
Ailia started to feel tired and she thought it would be best to head home and get some sleep. Searching the heavens, Ailia sighted a shooting star in the pitch-black, light-speckled sky. The Auroras hadn’t shown themselves recently and she wondered if her mother was still looking down upon her, guiding her steps through life, helping her onto unseen, privileged paths. 
Out here in the dark, she was alone, yet strangely enough, not lonely. Ailia headed toward Brandersgaard and tried to clear her mind of all the questions life had recently thrown at her, insurmountably difficult questions she had no answers to—at least not yet. She could go crazy thinking about them, searching for the answers that life so slowly rewarded. Life on the farm had not been easy, but one thing Uncle Brander and Aunt Unni had taught her, something she was truly grateful for, was to value work. 
She was embarrassed to admit, even to herself, that several times when asked to help, when she was blossoming into adulthood, Ailia had declared her independence, saying that Unni and Brander were not her real parents, so how could they order her around?  Ailia liked to think that her remorseful and quick attitude adjustment was proof of her maturing, but it probably had a lot more to do with her having to sleep outdoors in the pigsty and not having the privilege of a meal. She smiled as she remembered the ‘old’ Ailia. Finally, she arrived home. Right as she was about to enter through the front door, she heard someone call her name.
“Ailia?” 
A chill went through her spine. She could recognize Soren’s voice anywhere.



22

A Healer Returns

“Soren!” Ailia fought to contain the irrepressible joy that welled up inside of her. She stepped closer to him and though she didn’t feel she could or should embrace him, even though that was what she wanted, she stroked his shoulder and arm to greet him.
“You look well,” Soren said, smiling at her. He looked happy to see her too. “Something is different with you,” he continued, his eyes searching hers. He looked different too. His skin was sun-kissed, and the stubble on his face was a little lighter than the black it had been before. 
“Different?” Ailia said, pretending not to know what he meant. How will I manage to not tell him? Improvise. “My foot is all healed. Thank you, again, for your help,” she said, ignoring his prodding, redirecting the conversation to safer subjects. Ailia couldn’t remember blatantly lying before and she felt very uncomfortable concealing the truth from the one she loved, if she dared say, so dearly. This is going to be hard if Soren continues to ask similar questions as the first one.
 “So—any more wolf chasing?” Soren asked jokingly.
Ailia laughed. “No. I knew you were away, so I thought I would refrain from such adventurous activities.”
Soren chuckled. “It is really good to see you again,” he said sincerely. He took a step closer and gave her a big bear hug. 
Ailia hugged him back and she leaned her head into his chest. Her mind raced with all the information she had learned over the last few months. Now that she knew the truth about who she was and about who he was, she felt calm and peaceful, yet still wanting to jump up and down for joy. A feeling of completeness finally overwhelmed her incomplete, yearning heart. When can I tell him?
Soren’s body tensed and he sighed, like he had felt something for Ailia, but knew he could not act on it. He slowly pulled away, his arms still wrapped around Ailia. 
Ailia looked up into his blue eyes. He seemed to draw her in closer with each glance, each breath and each word. She stood speechless for a moment, trying to read him. 
Soren let go of his grip and stepped back. “So, I am curious, did you ever figure out how you ended up in the middle of nowhere?” he asked.
“No, it’s an enigma. It’s like I lost four months of my life,” Ailia said. “Oh, I did find— a—” She stopped.
“A—?” he gently nudged her.
She wanted to make sure she didn’t share information she wasn’t supposed to, but decided it couldn’t hurt to tell him about the handkerchief and flask. “—Raven embroidered handkerchief, so we have reason to believe that the—uh—the Vikings had something to do with my disappearance,” she said, stumbling over her words. “An empty glass flask.” She had a hard time concentrating on anything other than the fact that Soren was standing right in front of her. “Can we talk about something else?” she finally said. “I’m just having a hard time. I don’t know; I just cannot say too much.”
 “About what? Are you trying to hide something from me?” he asked and smirked.
“No!” she nearly yelled and shook her head fervently. She resisted every temptation to think or say anything about him and her.
Soren scratched his eyebrow as it arched up and laughed under his breath. “All right, so, I heard Lucia is here?” he said. “I came as soon as I found out. No one sent for me, not even Silya. I thought that was strange.”
“Yes, she is here,” Ailia said in an unhappy tone, not willing to clarify anything else. She desperately wanted to tell him who she was and that it was her, not Lucia, that was his Sentinor, bound together since the beginning of their spirits’ creation. She bit her lip. She couldn’t let him go just yet, so she changed the subject again. “How were your travels down south?”
“They went really well. Mumtaz is gathering the elders who will in turn help us get the armies we need. Once the Great Sentinor is ready, the armies will cross the Orken Desert to get here. It will be a challenge to have all the troops cross the desert when it is time, so a lot of planning is needed,” Soren said.
Ailia breathed heavily. How am I supposed to be their leader? I know nothing of troops or armies, or anything! They won’t follow me. She felt like she was going to have a panic attack.
Soren didn’t seem to notice her distress. “Ailia, the devastation down south is just horrific. We think we have it bad here, but it is so much worse down there. Can you imagine living without access to clean water, being swarmed by bugs the size of my hand?” Soren said, lifting his hand up to show her. “People lie dying in the streets without anyone to help them and the only food they have are grains since nearly all their animals have died of some disease. Fortunately, they are still able to harvest plants and grains, but it will not be long until there is nothing left.”
“I’m sorry. Is there any way I can help?” Ailia asked, feeling compassion well up in her bosom. She knew she needed to complete her plan, but she had absolutely no idea of where or how to even start.
“Not yet, but eventually we will need everyone’s help to defeat Eiess. Once Lucia finishes her plan, for it has to come from her, we will be ready to attack.”
“All right, I understand,” she said, nodding her head anxiously, taking his statement to heart.
“I also visited my—descendants,” Soren said.
“Oh,” Ailia said, slightly interested, nodding her head. “Oh!” She hadn’t thought about the fact that she had descendants. She felt guilty immediately.
“The youths call themselves Quartz.” Soren laughed. 
“Quartz?” 
“Yes. They gave themselves that name, being descendants from Lucia and myself. As you know, Lucia and I are both demi-mortals, but they are not. They do have certain endowments within them, unique gifts that are supernatural, but not as much as Lucia and I. So they thought instead of calling themselves demi-mortals, which they are not, they would go by quarter-mortals, or Quartz for short. Clever, right?” Soren said.
Ailia looked at him without responding. All this was too much to take in at once, plus she already struggled in trying to hide her identity. She had just gotten used to admitting she was the Great Sentinor and now she had to hide it again from the one person she really wanted to tell.
“Are you sure you are all right?” Soren asked, seeming very concerned for her well-being. “You are acting very strange. Did you have too much mead, maybe?”
“No. I—I’m sorry.” Ailia exhaled sharply. She decided to be as honest as she could, without divulging everything she needed to keep secret. She was not doing a very good job at ‘acting’ normal, or like the old, peasant Ailia. She breathed heavily again. There had to be a way she could be honest with him without breaking her vow of silence. “There is something,” she said, looking away. “ I cannot tell you what it is. You need to trust me on this.” Ailia turned toward Soren again. She took his hand and looked up into his eyes, finally letting her guard down. “Will you trust me—please?” she asked.
“Yes,” Soren said without hesitation in his voice. “Yes, I will trust you.” 
They stood looking at each other for a moment, communicating in silence. Ailia felt that he truly did trust her. A friendship had been taken to the next level. “Thank you. I’m so relieved. I worried you wouldn’t. I cannot keep up with all the changes that are going on in my life, a new sister, new information—” Ailia said. She let go of his hand.
“Of course I trust you. Silya told me you are Lucia’s sister, which is wonderful. No wonder I felt there was something special about you.” He nudged her.
“Ah, yes,” Ailia said and smiled on the outside, but cried on the inside. If he only knew.
“Are you getting to know each other better?” 
“Yes, we are and we have so much in common. It’s been a very exciting season here in Bergendal. Someday, I’ll tell you all about it. I promise.” Soon, Ailia hoped.
“Well, I know you would probably like to stay out here all night, but I am anxious to get inside to the heat,” Soren said finally. “Besides, there are Surtorians lurking around every corner and I would rather not get noticed by one.”
Ailia felt foolish. She hadn’t thought about the fact that Soren had just come travelling from heaven knows how far and she was keeping him outside and also keeping him from Lucia. “Oh, sorry, I was just so happy to see you again. Of course you should be getting inside.”
“I love your humbleness,” he said, following her through the door.
They stepped into the foyer and removed their overcoats. The little light they had to brighten their path shone from the hearth in the main room. Ailia instinctively took Soren’s hand and guided him, so he wouldn’t trip on anything. 
“Follow me,” she said, leading him to the hearth. “This should help you warm up.” She picked up firewood and placed it onto the dwarfed flames. “Can I get you some leftover stew? Unni is a great cook,” she offered.
“Yes, thank you. That sounds delicious,” Soren said.
“Please, have a seat,” Ailia said, gesturing toward the bench.
He sat down slowly at first and then with a low thump. The modest amber light from the fire burned low, illuminating his serious face. 
“I must admit that I felt really bad leaving so abruptly with no explanation,” Soren said. 
“It’s all right. I made it home safely,” Ailia said.
“No, but I really feel that we met for a reason. There is something about our friendship that is different, would you not agree?”
Ailia stood speechless.
“Will you forgive me?” He looked so sincere, and kindness exuded from his narrow eyes.
“Yes, of course,” Ailia said without hesitation. She couldn’t help but smile. He had felt something, but he didn’t know what Ailia knew yet. Once she told him, it would all make sense to him too. 
Ailia took out a small wooden bowl and scooped the stew into it and then handed it to Soren. 
He sat and ate in silence for a few moments. “So, tell me about your journey back here. Anything happen?” Soren asked quietly.
“No. The trip was great and I absolutely adore Silya. She’s a gem. She told me how you two met and filled me in on more information about the Sentinors and Eiess and the Aesira Jewel. It’s all very fascinating,” she said, still pretending to be an outsider.
“Silya is one of the wisest women I know. She has had a rough life, but instead of growing angry and bitter, she has taken the hardships of life and molded each lesson into diamonds of great wisdom.”
“I agree. She is very wise. Did she travel with you here to Bergendal?” Ailia asked.
“Yes. I actually was not planning on stopping by,” Soren said reflectively, scooping the last spoon of stew out of the bowl. “Silya insisted I did, but I was stubborn. Then she told me Lucia was here and I had to come right away. Is she sleeping?”
“Yes,” Ailia said. “You want me to wake her?”
“No, she needs her rest. I will see her first thing in the morning.”
Ailia liked his answer. “So, are you here only for a day?” She didn’t want to hear the answer if that were the case.
“We will probably stay until the day after tomorrow and then Lucia will join Silya and I back to Trollsoe. We need to get her away from Eiess as soon as possible. I cannot believe Lucia is still here, so close to Eiess and that Eiess hasn’t found her yet.”
“Of course,” Ailia said. She felt like she could cry. Maybe if I approach him a little more directly, he will figure out who I am by himself, without me having to tell him and break my promise. She thought it was a dangerous plan and she liked it. In her desire to be chaste and save herself for the ‘one’, she had never approached a man in a manner like this. Her heart started pounding. Ailia squeezed in right next to him and placed her narrow hand on his knee, trying not to think of the rejection she might have to go through if he declined her.
Soren shifted slightly in his seat. “Ailia—” he said, freezing up and not looking at her. He exhaled. “I cannot be that for you,” he finally said, seeming as if he were struggling with the right words to say. “You know that, right?”
Ailia wasn’t willing to accept the rejection just yet. She lifted her knee up over his lap and sat down on his lap facing him. “I think you can,” she said and smiled.
Soren looked away. “I have felt an attraction to you and I cannot explain it. It does not make any sense, especially since my one eternal partner is someone other than you. I cannot give into a fleeting feeling like this one,” he said.
Ailia turned his face toward her, nudging him along. “Everything will be all right; just trust your heart,” she said. She wrapped her arms around his neck.
“No, you do not understand. I do not expect you to understand,” he said impatiently, shaking his head.
Ailia stood up and felt extremely embarrassed, not to mention rejected. “Why, because you think I’m not a demi-mortal?” she concluded, slightly offended. 
Soren stood up and looked her squarely in the eyes. “No, I admire you so much. There’s a strong force inside you that I cannot explain. It is almost like you are a demi-mortal, your energy is so strong.”
Ailia knew she couldn’t tell him about her true identity, not yet at least, so she decided to abandon her risqué plan of trying to seduce him. If she continued, she felt she would have to stoop too low and she was not strong enough to handle that kind of refusal from him. She walked away from Soren, embarrassed, and braced her chest with her arms.
To her surprise, Soren followed her. He came up close behind her and grabbed her shoulders, pulling her body close to his. His hands slowly made their way down Ailia’s arms and finally down to her hands, where they clasped hers in a tight grip. They stood there for a long time, their hearts beating steadily. Ailia leaned her head into his chest and he kissed her on the neck ever so lightly. She turned around and faced him and then they both embraced each other, holding on so tightly, afraid that if they let go, they might do something they both truly desired, but could not afford to do.
“I know this might sound outlandish,” Soren whispered. “But it is almost as if you—”
Ailia looked up into his eyes, hoping he would realize that she was the one he spoke of. “What?”
He stroked her hair, caressing it with his hand and then pulled it gently as he continued to kiss her neck and face. 
Ailia closed her eyes and enjoyed every touch, every kiss. She then started kissing him back, their lips still not joining. “Soren,” Ailia said longingly. Her body tingled and Soren stirred up feelings inside her that no other man had even come close to.
He seemed to enjoy hearing his name spoken from her lips and he cradled her face in his hands. 
He came in so close and Ailia could feel his breath on hers. Their eyes connected and Ailia could see that he really did feel something for her. His intensely blue eyes burned with desire and Ailia could see in them that he truly wanted her in that moment.
“No, not like that!” Brander said, over by the outer wall. 
Soren and Ailia froze, completely startled by the noise. They hastily stepped away from each other as if they were children who had been caught with their hands in a basket filled with fresh bread. Standing still for a moment, they listened. No sound.
“I think he is talking in his sleep,” Soren said. They both laughed silently. 
“Ailia?” Lucia said, suddenly appearing out of the darkness. She looked angry.
 “Oh, I am sorry,” Lucia said when she saw Soren. “Ailia, I thought you were alone. Hello, Soren,” she said and nodded to him. “What took you so long? I have been here for many months and you did not come for me.” She quickly turned around and walked away.
Soren looked as if he had seen a ghost. He massaged his temples, closed his eyes and sighed a painful sigh.
“This was a mistake,” he said. “I do not know what came over me. Ailia, I am—”
“Let me go talk to her,” Ailia said, trying to make it better without having him feel too bad about it. “I, I’m sorry. This was a bad idea. I’ll explain everything later; don’t worry,” she said and followed after Lucia.
 “Soren is here? Did you tell him?” Lucia asked, sounding somewhat dispirited.
“No, of course not. It’s not the right time yet. It kills me that I cannot tell him, because I just want to be with him. And what’s worse than that is that I don’t know how long it will be until I can tell him. It could be weeks, months, years—or worse, even decades,” Ailia whispered, letting out a groan.
“Oh, it will not be decades,” Lucia said. “I am sure it will be sooner than you think.”
“Thank you,” Ailia said half-heartedly. She couldn’t expect Lucia to really understand or even sympathize with her predicament. Immediately, she felt guilty for thinking that. “I’m so grateful I have someone to talk to about this—it helps a lot.”
Lucia smiled faintly. “So, what am I supposed to do?” she asked, looking self-conscious. “I would feel weird pretending to be, well, you know, you,” she gestured to Ailia and sat down on her bed. 
Ailia hadn’t thought about how this would affect Lucia. Lucia would have to go along with being the Great Sentinor, acting as if she were Soren’s—Ailia didn’t like thinking about it. It wasn’t like Lucia loved him, or even that Ailia didn’t trust her on this subject, but she did start to have feelings of jealousy well up unexpectedly inside her and she didn’t like the unwelcome emotion. How should we handle this? They hadn’t really talked about it, not knowing when Soren would come back. 
“I think you need to—uh—I guess, pretend you are me,” Ailia finally said, coming to the conclusion that it was the best plan. For Lucia couldn’t avoid him and act as if she wasn’t interested at all, for that would become plain awkward for everyone involved. Or, maybe a better plan would be that Lucia could try and convince Soren to leave again. She abandoned that plan as quickly as she thought of it. Her mind was starting to conjure up ideas on how to make it less painful for her in the short term. In the long run, this short time will not matter. When Soren and I are married and I have defeated Eiess, Lucia, Soren and I will look back at this time and laugh—or so she hoped. 
“I am not a very good performer, you know,” Lucia said. “Are you sure this is the best way? I do not want to not help you, but it feels so strange. What should I do when he tries to kiss me?” Lucia asked. It seemed she was going over all the details in her head.
It was a valid point. Ailia hadn’t thought through this too well and she wished she could talk to Unni about it some more before they jumped into role-playing. She remained steady in her decision. The answers would have to come along the way. “It’s the best way and I have complete confidence and trust in you, Lucia. Please do this. I know it is going to help tremendously. The most important thing is that we keep this information as unrevealed as possible,” Ailia said. “Now, he wants to leave the day after tomorrow to Trollsoe—with you. You are going to have to go with him if he insists, or if we cannot sway him from leaving.” It tore Ailia up inside that he would be leaving again, but she couldn’t think about that now when so many other things were at stake.
Lucia leaned forward, sitting on both her hands. “Ok, I will do my best. I hate to see you struggle with this,” she said. “Maybe, I could insist you come with me since you are my sister?”
Ailia raised her eyebrows and peered over at Lucia. “Now, there’s a thought.” She paused, bringing index finger in front of her lips in a thinking pose. “Let’s sleep on it and talk again tomorrow,” she said, her hope renewed.
“Good night,” Lucia said.
“Yes, good night and thank you,” Ailia said and hugged her sister before jumping into bed.
Ailia’s mind continued to race with the day’s events. She anxiously waited for the morning when she would see Soren again, but she feared the awkwardness of their illusion would make life intolerable in the short term. Ivanka’s forewarning hung annoyingly around in the back of Ailia’s mind as she tried to go to sleep. She hoped that Ivanka had been wrong. She was probably just a crazy fortuneteller anyway, or a crazy old hag. Still, something told her that there was some truth to her terrifying foretelling. Finally, sleep took her and it was, thankfully, a dreamless night.



23

A Change of plans

All were still sleeping, dreaming and worry-free, at Brandersgaard when Ailia arose early next morning. Ailia’s mind wouldn’t rest and kept churning and winding, provoking her heart with bothersome thoughts. What if it doesn’t work? What if Lucia betrays me again? What if Soren loves Lucia? What if—? Fear had come knocking, worming its way into her mind and Ailia didn’t know how to let fear stay outside, feeling forced to open to its piercing demands. 
This was the first time Ailia could ever remember being up before Unni, who usually rose to light the hearth if it had gone out at night, or increase its blaze if it hadn’t. The flames were still aglow, bringing with them the only physical warmth the Northlandic Kingdom had seen in all too many months and the seasons were not about to return to normal any time soon. She saw that Soren had fallen asleep next to the hearth. Her stomach fluttered at the sight of him.
Ailia wrapped a reindeer fur throw around her and quietly stepped outside, looking to the black, star-speckled heavens. The dry snow creaked below her feet with each step. 
“Mother?” she beckoned, seeking loving advice from the spirit realm. “I feel so lost. I don’t know what to do. It seems like every choice I make ends up in a dead-end. I feel I cannot move in the direction my heart tells me. If I tell Soren who I am, we may all be in more danger, but I feel I need his strength to move forward.” She walked casually over to the stable and entered where Volomite was standing. He wasn’t asleep either. “Hey you, good to see you again.” Ailia brushed his cold, black mane. 
He nickered, pawing his hoof on the straw-covered, mud-packed floor below and moved his head to greet her. 
“I missed you too.” Ailia placed her hands on his face and stroked him calmly down his neck toward his well-developed shoulder. She let him go and strolled over to gather some eggs from the chicken cage. 
They used to have dozens of chickens, but now, they were down to a measly seven after having lost them to the frost. Brander had mentioned that he wanted to bring the fowls inside the main house before they all froze to death. In the beginning, Unni was fervently against it, not wanting those “incessantly chirping creatures” inside, but now she realized that if they stayed outside for much longer, they would not have any chickens or eggs left. Ailia picked up seven eggs, put them in the wicker basket next to the pen and started toward the house again. Scrambled eggs for breakfast sounds delicious. 
As she looked into the heavens again, she saw the Auroras gleaming brightly across the sky. Her mother was listening. Now it was time for Ailia to see if she could hear her mother calling from the grave, bestowing wisdom upon her spirit by speaking to her heart. Ailia stood still for a moment, waiting for a revelation. 
“Please, Mother, please tell me what to do with Soren. Should I tell him?” she whispered, closing her eyes, turning inward, but not receiving any communication other than her own thoughts, which were, It’s too cold to stay out here. I guess I’m weaker than I thought. 
Ailia flung the reindeer throw onto the bench as she entered the front foyer. She heard movement from inside the house and it looked like Unni had awoken and breathed new life into the hearth and was working in the kitchen.
“I saw Soren came in last night?” Unni whispered, looking up at Ailia as she entered.
“Yes,” Ailia confirmed, seeing that he was still sleeping by the hearth. She placed the eggs on the table and then huffed.
“What’s wrong? I can recognize that huff anywhere. You’re fretting over something,” Unni whispered.
“It’s nothing.” Ailia thought about not bothering Unni with her problems, but she then quickly changed her mind. She needed a trusted confidant now more than ever. “Well, actually, I’m just having a rough time adjusting to be—the real me and then not being able to say anything to—Soren,” she said in a low voice.
“I see,” Unni said. “Tell me more.”
“The hardest part is pretending to be someone else and unfortunately, I’m not pretending very well.” Ailia leaned her hip against the table and crossed her ankles and arms where she stood.
“I’ve been thinking about it as well and I think the wise choice would be to include Soren, even if telling him is potentially more dangerous. The more right people we have for us, the better off we’ll be. We will just have to be more careful in how you two interact in public. As far as we all know, Eiess still believes Lucia is the Great Sentinor and we need to use that fabricated reality to its fullest potential.”
“And that too, I just feel so bad that Lucia has to take all the risk here. I feel like she resents me for it and I cannot blame her. If Eiess discovers where Lucia is hiding, she would kill her in an instant and then I would lose my only sister. She’s all alone, risking her life for me,” Ailia said.
“Well, that simply isn’t true, Ailia. If she doesn’t help, Eiess will come after you, killing you for the third and final time and everyone will perish by Eiess’s hands or live as thralls, in fear and bondage forever. You cannot take upon you someone else’s responsibilities in life, not even your sister’s. Each has to pay their own dues and find their own way.” Unni walked over to Ailia and placed her hand on her shoulder, looking her in the eyes. “I’m sure she is happy to do this for you and for everyone.”
“I know, but I still feel so—guilty.” Ailia pivoted away from Unni.
Unni placed her fists on her hips, her strict eyes staring Ailia down. “Ailia,” she said, agitated. “Drop the guilt, drop the worry, because it doesn’t serve anyone. Guilt is only there for misery’s benefit and if you hold on to it, it will decrease your strength. There is no other purpose for guilt than to correct an error, before you choose to err or after you have done it.” Unni looked around the room as if she was searching for something. “There is no error here,” she said, her hands and shoulders lifting up.
“I suppose—” Ailia started.
“Ah—” Unni stopped Ailia, her palm facing away from her.
Ailia sighed in annoyance. “Ok, I understand,” she finally said, rolling her eyes.
“I mean it,” Unni said strictly, with the same look Ailia had seen hundreds of times growing up, when she knew something was to be taken seriously. 
Ailia slowly broke a smile. “I do, I understand.” She laughed. She was glad that Unni would still help talk her through the difficult times. Unni had always been a wonderful mother, listening to her most inner thoughts. She had a gift for listening and helping the solution come to light. Now, more than ever, Ailia needed her pearls of wisdom. 
“So, what’s for breakfast?” Brander interrupted. “Serious stew?” He laughed at his own joke. 
“Scrambled eggs,” Unni and Ailia said in unison. They looked at each other and smiled.
“Great, I will take three,” Brander said, fastening his belt around his shirt, still getting dressed for the day. “I’ve been losing some muscle lately and I need the meat.”
“Oh, no you won’t,” Unni said sassily. “Not until you finish building that indoor chicken coop we’ve been talking about.” 
Brander looked at Ailia. “What mare demons visited her last night?” He winked at Ailia.
Ailia tried to remain serious but couldn’t help smiling.
“May I help get breakfast going?” Lucia said, looking all pretty and ready for the day. “I am starving!” Her wavy long, blond hair was brushed and she had put a dried flower over her ear.
“You look lovely today, Lucia,” Brander said.
“Well, Soren arrived last night,” Lucia said and smiled, almost acting giddy.
Was she playing her part really well, or was there something in her mannerism that gave the impression that she actually liked Soren? Ailia brushed the thought away quickly. Lucia had promised she would never betray her again.
Unni pointed toward the table with the pots and pan and looked at Ailia. “Fetch the pan. I’ll ready the omelet.”
Breakfast was prepared and devoured in a hurry. Soren had left right after breakfast with Lucia to pay Bishop Peter a visit. He said he’d be back by mid-day.
Today was a big day in Bergendal and no one wanted to miss any of the festivities that were held during the Late Summer Festival. Of course, the events had changed since its inception, not to mention the weather.
“I have decided to speak to Soren after the event tonight,” Ailia told Nora as they finished cleaning up after the meal.
Nora nodded, as her eyes blinked fervently, like they always did. Her wrinkled face had shriveled up nearly beyond recognition, with deep lines grooving into her leather-looking skin. It was as if she had aged overnight. She had lost one of her front teeth since she had arrived at Brandersgaard and her hair had thinned and whitened to a soft silver—like an angel’s. 
“I think you are right. It is wise that we include Soren. Though, there is much danger associated with him knowing the truth, we can definitely use his strength at this time,” Nora said, drying the pan slowly with her crinkly spotted hands. “Just make sure he is fully sober when you tell him,” Nora laughed. “You will want him to remember it in the morning.”
 “He doesn’t seem like a man who is too fond of drinking mead or wine, so he’ll still probably be clear of mind toward the end of the evening,” Ailia said. “But just in case, I will make sure Lucia keeps an eye on him for me.”
After her chores were finished, Ailia went into the rearmost room and laid out her special blue Sunday dress on Unni and Brander’s bed. Her ivory, long-sleeved, ankle-length underdress looked quite frayed and old, lying there next to the new blue over-dress, but it would have to do. It wasn’t like she had another one to choose from. 
Everyone had left the house to either run errands or to do chores outside and Ailia seized the opportunity for a bath. She filled the largest cauldron with melted snow, putting it on the hearth to heat. Once heated, she then took it into the back room and set it down on the floor. 
Unni, who had recently been dubbed the best housewife in Bergendal, kept a neatly filled supply of linens and washcloths inside the wood pantry. Ailia grabbed the top washcloth and laid it on the cauldron’s thick upper edge. She undressed and started to bathe. Her last full body bath had been on their designated bath day—Saturday. Today was Thursday, named after the god of thunder, Thor. 
Washing her body, she blushed as she imagined what it would be like if Soren touched her bare skin on all the places that her clothes normally covered. She had never been with a man before in that way, a fact she was rather proud of. 
A creak in the flooring made her turn around and cover herself as best she could with the washcloth, suspecting there was someone there. 
Ailia turned around and spotted Soren. Their eyes met briefly, but Soren quickly averted his eyes. “I am sorry, Ailia, I thought no one was here,” he said, turning away. “I left a— something here.”
Ailia didn’t know quite what to do. She wanted him to see her as she was, but not yet, not like this. “It’s fine, Soren,” she spoke calmly. “I know you didn’t mean it.”
He excused himself and dashed out of the house. 
I wish he knew already, Ailia thought. After her bath, she dressed and thought she looked decent enough for the night’s events. 
Unni and Sigrid had returned from helping Brander slaughter the evening’s main course: Lotte the pig. Ailia had picked up a bad habit of naming all the animals on the farm. She hated it anytime any of her ‘children’ were slaughtered, even though she fully realized that they needed the food. Busily, they scurried to and fro, in and out of doors, preparing the master meal for the evening. 
As Ailia walked in with her gown, Unni did a double take at Ailia, dipped her hands in the water bowl, dried them on her apron and walked over to her. Unni swiveled her around. “Let’s go to the back again. I have something special I want you to wear for tonight’s event,” she said, her voice brimming with excitement. She led Ailia to the back room and opened the linen closet. 
Hurriedly, Unni searched through the linen sheets and located what she was looking for. She pulled out a finely woven silk handkerchief, folded carefully around its mysterious contents. “Here you go.” She reached her arm out toward Ailia. “I wore this on the official day of my marital pledge, which it almost is for you. Well, the only difference is that I didn’t choose my husband to be. My parents did that part for me. Thankfully, they did a pretty good job. But never mind that, this is your special day. Here.” Unni reached her hand forward more firmly.
Ailia accepted the bundle, knowing it would be a great insult if she didn’t. She peeled its exquisite edges apart until it opened. Inside were two shining Hatteberg bi-metal brooches. She gasped. Their complex design included six silver animal eyelet masks embellishing the upper circular border and domed golden bronze panels inlaid on the front. The triangular Valknut symbol was barely noticeable in the vine-like side patterns. Ailia had never seen anything nearly as beautiful in her entire life. Her fingers feathered the surface of the brooches. 
“Now, let me help you put them on,” Unni said, picking the brooches out of Ailia’s hallowed hand. “Oh dear, that under tunic will never do!” She looked in horror at Ailia’s ragged under tunic. “I didn’t want to give you this until later, but I think today is an absolute emergency.” She pulled out a stark white new under tunic that was embroidered with a detailed blue thistle pattern at the sleeves and skirt hem. “Here you are, dear. Now hurry and change. I have repast to prepare.” 
After Ailia changed, Unni helped her attach the brooches, along with strings of beads that attached between the brooches in red, green, brown, yellow and silver. Ailia had never felt more beautiful. Now, she felt ready to approach Soren. 
“Come with me and help set the table. Don’t worry about preparing the food. I wouldn’t want you to get your dress dirtied,” Unni said, ushering Ailia with her.

*    *    *

Silya, who had been invited to repast, arrived with Soren and Lucia. She was going to spend the night with them before the three left in the morning. 
“Repast is ready!” Unni hollered from the kitchen. The long table had been pulled out and set in the main room between the hearth and the kitchen. The Late Summer Festival repast was the fanciest meal Ailia had seen all year. At the center of the table sat the roasted pig still intact with all its limbs and body parts. Brander had been roasting the beast outside all day and its aroma filled the entire room, flirting with their taste buds and hungry bellies. Bread, carrots and potatoes, which were considered luxury foods in these times of dearth, were all laid out on the table in plenty. Abundant amphorae filled with mead and even wine had been allotted for the day’s events and none in the house would leave without being a little cheerier. 
 “A toast to all guests and especially our beautiful women,” Brander said, raising his glass at the end of the table. 
Everyone stood by their seats at the overly crowded table and rose their glasses. “My cheer, your cheer, all the pretty women’s cheer!” they all chimed in. 
Unni sat at the other end, with Ailia, Ivar, Sigrid, Silya and Nora on one side. Soren, Lucia, Bishop Peter and his Deacon, Anders, sat at the other side. 
Ailia noticed that Soren kept looking over at her several times throughout the meal. Was it because she looked nice in her dress?  Or, maybe he was thinking about how he had walked in on her earlier when she was taking a bath?  She hoped so. 
Lucia looked perfectly happy sitting by his side at repast; she played her part well. Almost too well, Ailia thought. All through the evening, Ailia noticed how Lucia would brush her hand lightly over Soren’s. She’d smile at him, flirt with him and it looked like she was touching his knee under the table. 
Before repast, Ailia had pulled Lucia aside and spoken to her about bringing Soren to the storytelling tent before the first reading. “Make sure he does not drink too much mead,” Ailia had said and laughed.
“Of course not. He will be sober as ever,” Lucia had said and skipped off to be with him.
Ailia didn’t think Lucia was taking this seriously enough and didn’t know if she had even understood what Ailia had said. All throughout the meal, Ailia noticed that even though Soren seemed to return Lucia’s affection outwardly, he had the slightest expression of awkwardness in his eyes as they moved from place to place, never finding rest. 
“More potatoes, Ailia?” Unni prodded. She handed her the potato bowl.
“No, thank you,” Ailia said, passing it on to Ivar. He looked remarkably well-groomed tonight, handsome even, for a man of his age.
“But, you’ve barely eaten anything,” Unni said.
“I’m just excited for the festivities, that’s all,” Ailia said, picking at her food with her eating knife.
“Maybe some carrots then?” Ivar pitched in.
“I’m good, thank you,” Ailia said, refusing the bowl and gulping some more mead. “More mead?” she asked.
Unni was about to object.
“Here you go.” Brander was quickly by her side, winking at her. “One more won’t do any harm.” 
It wasn’t that Ailia was not hungry, or that the food didn’t look absolutely mouthwatering, she just didn’t have room for anything other than the jittery butterflies in her stomach. Ailia kept rethinking her plan, even though she felt happy about it. She had decided that after she had met up with Soren and Lucia in the storyteller’s tent, Ailia would take Soren to Bergendal Stave Church and open her heart to him, explaining who she really was. I hope I’ll say the right words, so he understands. As long as Lucia vouched for her, her plan should work. She finished off the rest of her mead and smiled over at Soren. Their eyes locked for a moment and the butterflies in Ailia’s stomach returned. He looked so handsome in his fancy blue tunic. It really brought out his eyes and complemented his dark hair. 
“Well, we best be off to the festivities,” Lucia said, rising to her feet.
“But, there’s still dessert,” Unni objected. “You must stay for dessert.”
“We will be back for it later.” She grabbed Soren’s hand and pulled him with her.
Soren followed her lead and thanked Unni and Brander for the wonderful meal. “We will see you all at the festival,” he said, glancing at Ailia again.
Lucia wrapped her arm around him and they left.
“I don’t like the way she is flirting with him,” Unni said. “Not one bit.”
“We spoke just last night. I’m sure she is just playing her part really well,” Ailia hoped, but now she had started to doubt her sister’s loyalty, seeing how forward she had been with Soren at the table. “Don’t you think?” she said hesitantly.
“Well, you better keep an eye on that one,” Brander said. “She’s a little too flirtatious in my opinion.”
“Lucia is as honest and full of integrity as the day is long,” Nora said. “If she said she is going to do something, she will.”
“I sure hope so for her sake. If not, she’ll have to deal with Unni and my wrath,” Brander said, not joking. “And no one should ever have to be in that merciless position.”
Ailia braved a smile, though without as much confidence as she would have liked. “I’m sure everything will be just fine. We have a plan and we are going to follow through. Besides, what could possibly happen?” A whole lot, the answer came to Ailia’s mind. A whole lot.



24

Treachery

“Their ugly, brown faces peered at them with black eyes. These skraelings, ugly men, brutally attacked the Vikings in Wineland, the land they had themselves claimed when they sailed their ships to this mystical land. Halvor the Red headed the dangerous expedition after being banned from Frostland for manslaughter. He established Bratthild estate with the men and women—”
Ailia sat in the back row on the benches listening to the storyteller’s gripping tale of the Viking excursion to Vinland and beyond. Many times, Ailia had wanted to explore an unknown world such as the one the storyteller had been to, adventure being the name of the game. 
Looking through the crowd, Ailia didn’t see Lucia or Soren anywhere. “Be here before the storyteller starts,” she had told Lucia. How could she have misunderstood her?  Maybe they got lost? But, she knew that now she was just making excuses for her sister.
“—finally, they were victorious over the devil-faced skraelings. It was even Guro, Halvor’s half-sister, who was eight months pregnant with her firstborn, who overcame them! She had fallen behind the others, pleading for their help, but she could not keep up. She grabbed a sword from a man’s deceased body and plunged it into her own breast, frightening the others in—”
Ailia couldn’t concentrate on the story. She was too nervous, anxiously awaiting Soren and what was to be one of the most significant moments of the rest of their lives. Tonight, she would become his and he would see her for the first time in the light of the truth. And tonight, they would start their journey together to defeat Eiess. 
“—and that is why the Norse always win their battles.” The storyteller finished, rising to her feet in a glorious crescendo. Her braided blond hair looked lovely tonight, glowing like gold in the light of the lanterns.
The eighty or so people who sat and listened applauded warmly, roaring and whistling in delight. The merry crowd trickled out of the massive tent in anticipation of attending another event at the festival. Ailia didn’t see any of her former friends here and she was glad they hadn’t come to the storytelling. 
As people passed by, they were putting their masks on: some sheep, some cows or goats, even cats or dogs. Ailia would normally participate at the masked dance and would wear the sheep mask Unni had made for her, but her thoughts were not at all focused on the dance as they normally would be. She could not bear to tear herself away from the tent in case she would miss Soren. 
Outside she heard the fiddlers walking around the streets, spreading their merry tunes. The frightening memory of the Nukkern flashed through her mind and she cringed. I won’t be dancing to his tunes anymore. Ever since that day, she had hated the sound of any instrument that sounded like a fiddle. 
When Soren comes, I’ll ask him to come walk with me first and then we’ll go to the church. She liked her idea. Simple is good.
“Why, there you are!” Silya exclaimed. “I have been looking for you everywhere! Something has happened. You must come with me immediately back to Brandersgaard.” She took Ailia’s hand and hauled her along with her.
“What’s wrong?” Ailia asked, while trying to keep up with Silya’s increasing pace. “I cannot leave. I have to wait for Soren!”
“We cannot talk about it until we are back home, but yes, something is very wrong,” Silya said, panting as she ran.
“Is anyone hurt?” Ailia asked.
“No. Stop asking questions and focus on your pace. It is a time-sensitive subject and every second we wait is wasted, another second gone, another second to recover what is lost,” Silya said.
“Lost?” Ailia tried her very best to keep up with Silya, picking up her pace, moving her legs faster and lighter. Then, something unexpected happened. As she was thinking about what could have possibly occurred, the answer came to her. Ailia knew exactly what had transpired down to the smallest detail. She stopped abruptly, letting go of Silya’s hand.
Turning around, Silya looked at her. “What?” Silya said, acting very impatient.
“They left,” Ailia said, looking into Silya’s eyes for confirmation.
“Did you know?” Silya gasped surprised. “How did you know? Unni just discovered that all of their things are gone!”
“Just now,” Ailia revealed, the images and feelings still entering her mind. “I think I’m having a vision,” she said, her eyes wandering as clear impressions flowed into her thoughts. “Lucia has told Soren that I’m in love with him and that I’m trying to deceive him into believing that I’m the Great Sentinor. She convinced him to leave early, so it wouldn’t be as hard on me or embarrassing on him.” First irritation and then anger welled up in Ailia. “But why?” she questioned. “She’s going to ruin any chance I have of defeating Eiess. Doesn’t she realize that?” Ailia agonized as her heart was breaking, breaking for her sister’s betrayal and breaking for Soren.
“Let us not waste time here. Come with me back to your family, so we can make a plan. They probably left four to five hours ago, so they do have a head start, but we can still catch up with them if we hurry.” Silya gently took Ailia’s elbow in hers and started moving again.

*    *    *

At Brandersgaard, Unni came running toward Ailia as she came inside. “That deceitful young girl! She’s going to get it from me!” she blurted. “Did you know about this?” She turned to Nora, who had also just returned from searching for Ailia and gave her the evil eye.
“No, my lady.” Nora was able to maintain her composure. No one was going to ruffle her feathers. “This is completely unlike her. I am sure there’s a perfectly suitable explanation for all of this,” she said.
“Suitable? There would be no suitable explanation in all the nine realms of Yggdrasil that would suffice! We must do something quickly before we lose them forever. Who knows what Lucia will do to keep Soren away from Ailia? They may never return again.” Unni sighed as she paced around the hearth.
“Ailia said she had a vision. We may want to take heed in that,” Silya interrupted. “Did you see in which direction they were heading?”
“No, just that they were packing and getting ready. Lucia had convinced him to leave and he had agreed.” Ailia had also seen them embracing and kissing, but she was too devastated, too embarrassed, to share that information in front of everyone. Now, she started second-guessing herself. She had thought Soren liked her too, and she had sensed the strong connection between him and her. Maybe I have just been fooling myself. 
“I will ride after them. Most likely, they are heading to Trollsoe as they planned,” Silya figured. 
“They could have headed in any direction though, really,” Nora pitched in. “If Lucia truly does not want Soren to be reunited with Ailia, she could have changed their travel plans. She is a smart girl, but this surprises me. I am shocked to say the least. She is young and seemingly innocent that girl, but she does have a stubborn head on her shoulders, especially lately.”
“Only three main roads lead out of Bergendal: the northern, the southern and the western. We should send someone in each direction,” Brander said.
 “I’m almost certain that they are heading to Trollsoe,” Ailia said.
Silya answered, “I agree, but I think, to be on the safe side, we should send one rider in each direction. I will take the southern route toward Trollsoe. I am used to traveling alone and it will be faster for me that way.” 
“I will come with you,” Ailia said.
“No,” Brander said firmly. “You must stay here. It will be safest for you.”
Ailia was disappointed. “I’m not in need of protection!” she said, her voice shaking and angry. The last thing she wanted to do was sit here and wait for her fate to unfold.
Nora interjected. “Yes, Ailia, you are in need of protection from every source you can get. The first time you were killed by the hands of Eiess was when Soren was away. She drowned you in the fjord along with all your friends. The second time she got hold of you was also after Soren had left for a short trip. He had carefully planned everything out, so you would be safe, but Eiess’s powers had grown stronger than before and she had trained her Surtorians to track you down. They found you despite all your efforts and drowned you again. And today, Eiess is even stronger than before and we must all be at our guard at all times. When Soren finds out that you, and not Lucia, are his Spiritus Amor, we will need to increase the level of protection surrounding you tenfold. If you fail, Ailia, none of us will be safe and we will all suffer under the rule of Eiess. We cannot afford to let that happen, would not you agree?” 
Nora did have a good point and Ailia was convinced, though not happily.
“I’ll head west,” Brander said. “Toward Asker. I’ll ask Ivar to head north toward Hammerburg. He is familiar with the territory.” 
“Great, we have a plan. Now let us go before more time is wasted,” Silya said.
“May you all be safe in your travels,” Ailia said. “And thank you for your courage and willingness to support me. May we together conquer the destroyer.”


25

Betrayal 

“I still think it was unwise to leave in such a rush and not say farewell to anyone. I think they might get the impression that we are snooty and rude.” Soren sounded halfway serious, halfway joking as he glanced over at Lucia. 
They had been riding for several hours, heading southward toward Trollsoe, starting their long journey at the first sign of the cool blue winter night. The weather had been milder today, but not nearly amicable enough to melt any of the snow that blanketed the entire country and had for what seemed an eternity. Now, the distant sun had set in the west, behind the Tinden Mountains, after having burned the skies with red, orange and pink streaking clouds. The absence of the sun had ushered in the icy air, which crept and gnawed on Lucia’s body. 
“I like that we can spend some time alone together without everyone else,” Soren said. “It has been a long time since I have seen you,” he said. “You were just a youth last time.”
“I agree. I used to look forward to your visits, before—” Lucia did not want to go down that path, thinking of her father and mother. Their deaths were still too fresh in her bones, still tormenting her raw, mourning heart as only the death of one’s parents could. Their lies had not really made it easier for Lucia to let them go and in fact, it seemed that the pain of their deaths felt worse because they had deceived her.
 “I always looked forward to the day I could visit and you would be a young woman, no longer a girl,” Soren said, not backing down.
Lucia blushed as her eyes wandered away from him. He was being a little too forward, she thought.
“I am sorry, I did not mean to make you feel uncomfortable,” Soren said. 
Lucia turned to him and smiled. “You did not. I think I am just so used to being told no, not now, you are not ready yet and now I do not have those limitations anymore. This newfound freedom might take me some getting used to.” She removed a section of hair that had slid down her forehead and was playing with her lashes. Her blondish-white hair and fair complexion could mesmerize nearly any man she met, she had discovered and she used that to her every advantage with Soren.
 “I want you to know that you can take all the time you need. We do not need to rush into our relationship again. I remember you and I remember our past relationships, but this is all new to you,” Soren said. 
“Thank you,” she said. Lucia tried to be as sincere as she could. She briefly lifted out of her seat, trying to ease the numbness in her behind. “They will understand. We can always go back and visit after we are married,” she finally answered. An intense feeling of guilt sat and festered in her gut as a stale piece of bread, churning and making her slightly nauseated as she thought about it. Why had she done this? And how could she have betrayed Ailia again? She remembered having sworn to herself that she would never betray her own blood. 
Before, when Soren used to come visit her at the castle, when her life had been simple, she had been told that he was the man she would marry one day. Lucia had always had a deep respect for Soren and she believed that he was to be hers. It was not fair that Ailia, a sister she did not even know until recently, was going to steal away her husband-to-be. It did not matter that Lucia was not completely in love with Soren, yet. Time would make their love grow, she told herself. Besides, Ailia had not been very considerate toward her. She had never asked Lucia how she felt, or if she had any feelings for Soren. Ailia was too absorbed in her own problems to notice anyone else’s, especially any problems Lucia was going through. “I do not remember anything from—before,” Lucia said to Soren.
“What do you mean?” Soren asked.
“Well, I have lived two other times, right?”
“Yes.” Soren looked over at Lucia.
“I do not remember anything whatsoever from my first two lives—it is strange.” She hoped he would not see through her deception.
 “Well, as I recall, in your last life, you could not remember anything either until you were a little older.”
Lucia felt relieved. So, it was true that she could not remember. Now, she did not need to try to conjure up their old memories.
“It will come back to you sooner or later. Later, in your second life, you started having dreams of our first life together. You dreamt of certain important moments,” Soren said.
“Really?” Lucia was baffled. Ailia had not mentioned any dreams to her, but then again, maybe she had not had any yet. Or maybe she kept them from me. She could be as deceitful as my parents. 
“Have you had any dreams like that yet?” Soren wondered.
“No, none at all.” She grinned, lifting her eyebrows innocently. 
“Well, each life is different and each time I am excited to get to know you again,” Soren smiled. “You seem very different this life though, I must confess. I know you have been through a lot recently.”
“How do you think we should go about keeping everything secret?” Lucia asked. I do not want Eiess or her Surtorians coming after me. Had she been unwise in her plan?  She had tried to accept that her calling in life was to be a queen only and an honorary sacrifice for Ailia. Yet the more she had thought about her parents’ lies, the more their lies had bothered her. First, they had lied about her sister dying at birth and not only that, but they even lied about both their daughters’ identities. Then, her father had been unfaithful to her mother. What other lies could be waiting out there in the dark? If her own father could do this one thing to her mother, betraying her trust, exchanging it for heated nights with a whore, what type of man was he? If her mother could lie to her about who she was, what type of person was she? Her child-like love was tainted and the penetrating wedge in her heart had started to expand into a vastness of entitlement. I need happiness and I deserve to be happy, she told herself. I do not owe anybody anything, especially Ailia. 
“We need to be strategic about keeping it a secret. I thought maybe we could set up rules for when we are in public. We probably should not even be seen in public together at all after we arrive in Trollsoe. Eiess has her Surtorians out looking for us everywhere,” Soren said.
“Well, I will have you to protect me.” Lucia tried to flirt, tried to see if there could be a spark between them, but she still did not feel anything.
“I cannot always be there, but I will do my best when I am around. I will also have our grandchildren watch over you when I am away.” Soren seemed absent-minded.
“Wow, grandchildren,” she said. “So, what are our grandchildren like? You had mentioned them briefly earlier and I have not been able to stop thinking about them.” Lucia said. The partial lies came with greater ease now.
“They are wonderful, Lucia. You will love them the moment you meet them.” His face lit up immediately at their mention. “They call themselves the Quartz.”
“The Quartz?  Why that name?” Lucia asked, confused. 
Soren explained it to her and then added, “It was rather a long process before they agreed on their unofficial name. Everyone finally conceded to Solvei’s suggestion. She is the stubborn one, as stubborn and feisty as anyone I have ever met!” Soren laughed. “She is the daughter of Alva and Eira and is known in Trollsoe as the most beautiful girl in the city. Dangerously beautiful though, like Erlend Senior always says,” Soren said.
Lucia had heard mention of the demi-mortals before. She liked ‘her’ new identity. It was fitting for a princess.
“And then there’s Martin, son of Alva and Eira. He is an extremely gifted artist and has been painting for years.”
“What does he paint?” Lucia asked.
“Well, mostly portraits,” Soren answered. A faint smile shaded his lips. “He actually painted one of you, with me describing the way you looked in your first lifetime.”
“Did he capture me well?” Lucia asked intrigued.
“Yes, he did. It is almost like you are looking back at me from the painting.”
“Did I look much different, then?”
“Yes, very much so. The first two lifetimes you looked somewhat similar, but now, it is like you are another woman,” he confessed. 
Lucia felt a sting of guilt, but not as much as before. “Oh,” she said. “I hope that is not a bad thing.”
“No, of course not. It is you that I love, your heart, your mind, your spirit, not the exterior,” Soren said. “Though, you are very beautiful now too.”
Lucia looked at him, but then looked away quickly, feeling the burden surface in her eyes. “So any other grandchildren?” She wanted to completely purge the guilt. 
“Yes, there is Stina, Vidar and Erlend Junior, who are Liv and Otto’s three children. Stina is extremely well-educated and has an obsession with music. I will tell you more about that later. Then, Vidar is an outdoors type person. He loves to travel and set up camp outside in the back yard. And finally, there is Erlend Junior, the eldest of the youths.” 
“They sound like great youths,” Lucia said.
“They are.”
“Do they have any—gifts, as well?” Lucia had heard Ailia talk about that.
“You mean endowments?” Soren asked.
“Yes, of course. I apologize,” Lucia said, feeling embarrassed. No, not embarrassed, just nervous that he would see through her stories.
“Lucia, you do not need to apologize to me, ever.” Soren smiled and continued. “Solvei has magnified physical senses. She can hear and see things from a faraway distance. She can also sense smells well before everyone else. Martin has the gift of something we call ancestral evocation. He has the ability to contact a being who lived in the past, either a deceased family member or any person really.”
“So, could he contact me in a previous life?” Lucia wondered. That would not be good.
“I suppose he could. Now that would be a fun thing to try!”
“Well—” Lucia hesitated. “I suppose.” Knowing full well she would never allow it. 
“Stina has the gift and power to dull a person’s senses, by either putting them to sleep, easing their pain, or decreasing their sensory awareness,” Soren said solemnly. “And she has recently discovered that she can induce death by song.”
“So, she can kill someone by singing to them?” Lucia wanted to know more about that power and if she could learn to command it. 
“Yes, or about them; they do not even have to be there. Granted, she has only tried it on animals, but I am convinced that it works on humans as well,” Soren said.
“Can anyone learn this— endowment?” 
“No, it is an endowment one is born with,” Soren clarified. “Her gifts, if used wisely, may be valuable to us as we make our move on Eiess.”
“And what about Eiess?  I saw that she was able to control gravity. Is that all?” Lucia asked.
“Well, Eiess is more complicated. She has other endowments, as well, ones that she has developed over the past few thousand years. Technically, she is not considered a demi-mortal. She is an enigma. Her body, though it appears to be made of flesh and bones, is made of something else. We just do not know what,” Soren said. 
“But we are human, right?” Lucia asked.
“Halfway human. We are subject to human frailties and weaknesses, but we are not as easily killed off as a human. That said, if someone knows our weakness, we become an easy target. Drowning, for example, can only kill you. Eiess is well aware of that. If I were to light you on fire, you would not burn. You are Light, so anything pertaining to light will not harm you. Same with me, except I am the opposite of you. I can only die by fire, but not by drowning or anything else. I am a healer and since fire destroys all life, absorbing oxygen, which is the main source of healing, I cannot withstand fire. If Eiess ever finds out my weakness, she could kill me faster than a Viking kills his prey.”
“So, that is how I died before?” Lucia cringed, almost believing now that she was talking about herself.
“Yes, both times,” Soren said. His lips clamped closed, his jaw biting so hard together that the muscles protruded in his face. “The memory of your blue, prune-ridged body still haunts me.” 
“What about Eiess?” Lucia asked.
“What about her?” Soren said.
“Does she have a weakness?” Lucia wondered, leaning forward on her horse. Lucia did not want to admit it, even to herself, but she was slightly interested in getting to know the Empress more intimately. Eiess’s powers fascinated her.
“Well, Eiess is a tough nut to crack. She despises light and seeks the darkness, but she can still endure sunlight and heat very well without dying. It is almost as if she is immune to every element,” Soren said. “Have you had any inclinations maybe?”
“Uh, no, not yet.” Lucia shifted uncomfortably on her saddle. They rode on in silence.
Finally Soren spoke. “Are you hungry? If so, we can stop for some food.” 
“No,” Lucia responded assertively. She cringed immediately and hoped he had not noticed the stressed tone in her voice. Getting to Trollsoe was her only objective, so she could get as far away from Ailia as possible. “And what about Stina, Vidar and Erlend Junior?” she said, trying to keep his interest. 
“Well, Erlend Junior has part of the same endowment you have: seasonal manipulation. But his powers are not as developed or strong. He possesses another gift, the gift of discernment. He can read any person, not their thoughts really, but their intentions, their personality, their soul—”
That was not good news. “So, if he saw me and did not know who I was, would he be able to tell I was the Great Sentinor?” Lucia asked.
“No, his endowment is not that specific, though it has strengthened a lot recently as I understand. His endowment has more to do with reading and recognizing the person’s core or integrity, I suppose.”
Lucia breathed. As long as she did not associate too much with him, she thought she would be able to deceive him. “That is great,” she said, staring into the dusk.
“Vidar has the gift of environmental adaptation. Do not be surprised if you see him wearing nothing but a summer tunic in the middle of winter. He is not affected by weather. It is one of the most impressive things I have seen. He can also see perfectly well in all shades of darkness.”
“That would be a fun endowment to have,” Lucia said, laughing. “I think I would be playing some fun jokes on people. I just hope our grandson is not too interested in secretly watching young ladies undress.”
“Well—” Soren said. “He did it one time when he was thirteen, but he was caught and punished sternly by the young lady’s father.”
“What was the punishment?” Lucia wanted to know.
“He made him choose between undressing in front of everyone in his household or in paying him a silver coin every month until he turned eighteen.”
“Which one did he choose? Wait, I am going to guess he chose the easy way out,” Lucia said.
Soren laughed heartily, his head tilting back as he closed his eyes. He looked mischievously at Lucia. “He actually chose to pay up. He was so embarrassed after that, it made him think twice about ever doing it again.” A laugh escaped Soren’s lips again. Then, he turned more serious. “Of course I am not condoning his behavior. It was a big deal at Sorenhall. Liv was and still is to this day, appalled that her son would do such a thing. She raised them to be good Christian men, seeking after chaste women. You will like her,” Soren finished.
“Sounds like he learned his lesson,” Lucia said. Christians? Ugh! Lucia started thinking her new life with Soren might not be such a good fit after all.
“Yes. He will be done paying the young lady’s father in two years,” Soren said.
“Poor boy.”
Soren yawned. “If we ride on further for just another hour or so, we will arrive in Solnes and we will be able to stay indoors overnight. Does that sound like something you would like?” he asked.
“Absolutely!” Lucia said, excited to be out of the cold. She had never slept outdoors before, other than when she was waiting for Nora at the end of that wretched cold tunnel and it was not something she ever wanted to do again. She definitely considered herself an indoor girl. “There is so much I do not know. I am feeling a little overwhelmed at the moment.” Lucia felt concerned that her descendants would be the end of her.
“Anything I can do to help?” Soren offered.
“Well, just support me when I need it. I have a feeling I will be needing a lot of it,” Lucia said.
“I will be honored to.” He bowed gentlemanly on his horse and smiled at her.
She smiled back. He is so gullible, but a sweetheart, though.
They rode on for some time in silence, listening to all the sounds of the black forest night.
 “We should be arriving shortly at Solnes, the next small village. I know a family that will let us stay overnight. We should be seeing the lights from Solnes’s lit torches soon. Then, in the morning, we can travel on through the Small Mountains and Northland Forest before veering off to Hellsinker,” Soren said.
They kept on riding a ways, but no torches appeared in the distance. Without sound or warning, a little girl appeared, bloodied, walking with a blanket around her small frame. She could not be more than seven or eight years of age. Her big brown eyes looked up at Lucia and then Soren, her face serious, yet without emotion. They stopped their horses and Lucia jumped off immediately.
“Are you hurt?” Lucia asked, approaching the little girl. “Where are your parents?” she asked, looking around, as if she would be able to see them in the night.
The girl spoke no words but only stood in silence and stared at Lucia.
“What is your name girl?” Soren asked, descending from Volomite.
The girl took a step back and scowled.
“You are frightening her,” Lucia said to Soren. Turning to the girl, she said, “It is going to be all right, you will see.” She knelt down to be at the girl’s eye level. 
The girl’s lower lip pouted out as she closed her sorrowful eyes. A whimper escaped her bruised lips. 
“What happened to you, my sweet girl?” Lucia crept closer to the child in an effort to endear the child to her. “Will you whisper it to me?” Lucia held her arms out, welcoming the lost little angel.
The girl stepped closer and paused, looking as if she was thinking about whether or not she should say something, her eyes wanting to tell, but her fear probably holding her back. Her body shivered and a lonely tear mixed with blood skimmed down her cheek. She stepped closer to Lucia and leaned her head forward to Lucia’s ear.
“The Vikings are here,” she whispered.




26

Viking attack

After all the travelers had left Brandergaard, an eerie atmosphere lingered in the stuffy longhouse. Sigrid was eagerly weaving on the loom, which was situated in the corner by the back of the house. She quietly hummed an old Anglo-Saxon tune Ailia had heard her sing many times before. Its ghostly melody did not help lighten the mood. 


Let us all remember
All those that died that winter’s night
As we scurry on our path.
No one knew
That one kiss farewell would be their last

As they close the door
For all who are left behind, the memories haunt
 We still climb the tall mountains
Speaking of the pain of loss we share
The loss of those who live no more

Let us all remember
Our lives will not ever be the same
 We face the 
new world alone
Let us all remember
While the time slowly passes
We are all left behind to sorrow

Let us all remember
That winter's night became their final
As life continued on its eternal cycle
Do not forget
Some lives continue, yet for others
Today will be their last.

Ailia wasn’t sure if Sigrid had chosen that song intentionally, or if she was just singing it out of habit. It was a poor choice either way. 
Brander and Ivar had decided it be best if Ivar stayed to protect Ailia. Unni had travelled with the teenage neighbor boy to Hammerburg. It was unlikely that Lucia and Soren had headed in that direction, but it needed to be covered just in case. Hammerburg was only a two-day journey away on horseback, so Unni would be returning within the week if she couldn’t locate or track them down.
Ailia couldn’t sit still. She concluded that the best thing she could do was to clear her mind and try to find some more answers. Her mother’s grave was her preferred place to be when she needed to think and sort her thoughts out. Even though she knew that her mother was just as far away from her in her house as at the gravesite, she felt closer to her when she could see and touch the rune stone. She pulled her overcoat on, strapped on her boots and headed outside. 
Ivar was busy chopping firewood. He paused when he saw Ailia. “Where do you think you are headed, young lady?” he asked with no lightness in his voice.
“To the Bergendal Stave Church—uh—will you escort me perhaps?” Ailia asked.
“Yes, of course, my lady. This firewood can wait until later,” he said. He imbedded his heavyweight ax onto the giant log he was working on and proceeded to straighten out his clothes, brushing the sawdust off them. “Nothing like chopping wood to keep you warm—and foul-smelling,” he said, laughing. 
It was the first time Ailia had heard him try to crack a joke. She didn’t think his joke was funny at all; maybe that was why he didn’t open his mouth much. She tried to laugh, but her laugh came out sounding more like a whimper.
Ivar looked at her and nodded briefly. “Ready when you are, my lady.”
Ailia tried to sense if there was any animosity in his voice, but he sounded genuinely glad to help her. She wasn’t used to being waited upon. Her life had been one of service to others. Having someone serve her in this manner felt uncomfortably unfamiliar. She smiled at him, hoping she wouldn’t bore him with her company.
They started toward the church and walked in silence until Ailia finally thought of something that would be worthy of conversation. 
“How did you come to be employed at the castle for the king, uh, my father, I mean?” Even after all these months of knowing that King Olav was her father, Ailia still had a hard time accepting who she truly was.
Ivar looked at her briefly and almost smiled. “Well, I was a young lad, twelve, maybe thirteen, no definitely twelve, when my father died at the hands of his brother in a sword duel of honor. At the time, I was a very small boy, probably the smallest twelve-year-old in Asker,” he huffed. 
“My father was a very proud man, seeking honor and respect at any cost and he had become infatuated with the idea of being revered and in appearing upright in society. My uncle had a very jovial personality and had jokingly made a comment about me, something like I should have been born a girl—I was so small. It did not bother me much, but my father insisted he take the comment back and apologize to him in front of our chieftain. When my uncle refused, my father became furious and insisted on a duel between the two. It ended badly. I lost my father and my mother lost her husband, all in the name of pride and respectability.” Ivar looked into the horizon. 
“I vowed to live each day in an honorable manner, so I could gain the respect my father once sought. I felt it was the way to honor his memory. So, when King Olav announced a few years later that he was looking for young men to train for his guard, I eagerly traveled to Bergendal and signed up. By then, I had grown quite a bit, even rising above my uncle. I think he felt horrible the rest of his life for killing my father. He even took my widowed mother in after I left and fed her, clothed her and gave her a home until she died,” Ivar finished.
“And how did you come to be one of the king’s right-hand guards?” Ailia asked. She had no idea Ivar had such a sorrowful past.
“I did not know it at the time, but subconsciously, I set my own standards so high, even higher than what the king expected of me. I suppose he took notice and hired me to report to him directly. After that, I was finally promoted to the king’s chief guard,” Ivar said. His posture improved and the energy in his voice accelerated as he spoke.
“Quite an accomplishment,” Ailia said. 
“I was just doing my duty,” Ivar said.
“I would say it was more than that,” Ailia said. “I understand that my father trusted you completely. It’s a rare man who can be entrusted to such a level and I am sure my father considered you among one of his highest blessings. Every kingdom needs a good leader, but the leader needs support, needs to stand on the shoulders of grand men and women. Without them, the leader wouldn’t reach very high at all, I’m sure.” Ailia thought a moment about her situation. She needed to select the right people to help her through these coming times. That was the first step in her plan! Excitement grew in her bosom. She had known it all along, but she hadn’t been able to put it into words until now. She realized that it was important to prepare herself, but that it was equally important that she select and then prepare, her supporters, not just accept whomever was there. This became as clear in her mind as the burning sun on a bright summer’s day. Lucia’s betrayal is as deep as the ocean. Ailia sorrowed because she realized that she would never be able to trust her own sister completely again and that Lucia would not be a part of her future the way Ailia had envisioned.
They arrived at the Bergendal Stave Church right after the sun had descended below the mountains. Low-lying dense fog covered the white valley bringing with it a rather unwelcome frost and it became difficult to see even a few feet ahead. 
Ailia walked over to the familiar sight, the tall rune stone that stood erected in her mother’s honor. Each time she neared the burial place, an overwhelming feeling of nostalgia overcame her. Standing there beside Ivar in front of her mother’s grave, another thing finally dawned on her. She needed to start realizing her potential, her destiny and the force that she had been endowed with. The game which she was playing would only end the way she wanted if and only if, she stepped into it with both feet, grabbed it with both hands and saw it with both eyes. 
“Eyes see to the future,” Unni had always said. Now, she saw what was in front of her and no longer regretted what was behind her. The ending had already been established, the victory set up for her. Now, she needed to become worthy to claim it, to take it and make it her own. 
Her bosom burned with fervor, her heart felt strong and courageous, knowing that she was the Great Sentinor. She saw life as it was, like she had never seen before and it was hers for the taking, her right, her privilege. She looked over at Ivar standing so gallantly beside her, protecting her, serving her. She knew she must claim her rightful position and not live in excuses, nor fears, any longer.
“My lady,” Ivar said and knelt before her, bowing his head in a knightly manner. 
She thought it strange that he would bow to her here in front of the church. Then, she noticed that it had become lighter around her and wondered where the light was coming from. It was not a blazing light, nor a bright one, but a soft radiant glow and suddenly, she realized that it was coming from her skin.
